29:1066:68333:19:19:95:518:375:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:ness of the optimal seat-vote curve still dependsupon the degree of preference variation among
29:1067:68427:19:19:95:499:356:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:the Independents, but now also on the behavior of the second derivative of the loss function.
29:1068:68520:19:20:110:518:337:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:It should now be clear that the role of our assumptions concerning citizens’ preferences and the
29:1069:68616:20:19:95:518:317:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:distribution of Independents’ ideologies is to ensure that the optimal seat-vote curve has a simple
29:1070:68715:19:19:95:518:298:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:tractable form. This allows us to easily compute the values of the minimization and maximization
29:1071:68811:19:19:95:518:279:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:problems associated with the optimal inverse seat-vote curveΩ(io,io,V∗o(·)) andΩ(io,io,V∗o(·))
29:1072:68905:19:19:95:518:260:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:and hence derive the simple conditions for implementability presented in Proposition 2. More-
29:1073:68998:19:19:95:518:241:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:over, these assumptions permit the characterization of the optimal constrained seat-vote curve
29:1074:69092:19:19:95:518:222:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:by ensuring that the social welfare functionEW({i,i, V∗(·)}) has a relatively tractable form.
29:1075:69185:19:19:95:518:203:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:In this sense, our assumptions are key.  Nonetheless, they are not misleading because, as just
29:1076:69279:19:20:95:517:184:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:demonstrated, the determinants of partisan bias and responsiveness in the basic model remain in
29:1077:69374:20:19:95:517:164:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:more general models. Thus, the nature of socially optimal districting in more general models is
29:1078:69469:19:19:95:517:145:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:not going to be fundamentally different - it is just that additional considerations will come into
29:1079:69567:19:19:95:517:126:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:play. Obviously, understanding precisely how such considerations impact both the conditions for
29:1080:69662:19:19:95:518:107:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:implementability and the nature of the constrained optimal seat-vote curve is an interesting (and
29:1081:69759:19:0:103:461:88:36:g_d0_f8:65:g_d0_f9:25This assumes that the optimal Democrat seat-shareSolies betweenm(V)−τandm(V)+τ.
30:1082:69842:0:33:95:272:663:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:challenging) subject for further research.
30:1083:69884:33:29:95:196:630:209:g_d0_f3:209:g_d0_f3:9  Conclusion
30:1084:69897:29:19:95:517:601:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:This paper has developed a welfare economic analysis of the problem of districting. In the con-
30:1085:69992:19:19:95:517:582:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:text of a simple micro-founded model intended to capture salient features of U.S. politics, it has
30:1086:70090:19:19:95:518:563:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:studied how a social planner should allocate citizens of different ideologies across districts to max-
30:1087:70192:19:19:95:517:544:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:imize aggregate utility. Ideally, the social planner would like the Democratic seat share in the
30:1088:70288:19:19:95:517:525:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:legislature to be such that the social gains from marginally increasing it just equal the social
30:1089:70384:19:19:95:518:506:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:costs. Since changes in the parties’ aggregate vote share reflect changes in voters’ ideologies, the
30:1090:70484:19:20:95:517:487:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:optimal composition of the legislature will depend on the aggregate vote share. This yields the
30:1091:70579:20:19:95:517:467:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:key conceptual innovation of the paper - the optimal seat-vote curve. Under the assumptions of
30:1092:70673:19:19:95:517:448:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:the model, the optimal seat-vote curve is of the same simple linear form estimated in the early
30:1093:70768:19:19:95:518:429:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:empirical literature. Its “responsiveness” depends on the magnitude of the change in average voter
30:1094:70866:19:19:95:517:410:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:ideology signalled by a change in vote share, which in turn depends on the degree of preference
30:1095:70961:19:19:95:518:391:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:variation among Independents. Its “bias” depends on the difference in the fractions of Democrats
30:1096:71057:19:19:95:518:372:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:and Republicans in the population; specifically, it is biased in favor of the party with the largest
30:1097:71157:19:19:95:155:353:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:partisan base.
30:1098:71171:19:20:110:517:334:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:If there exists a way of districting voters that makes the equilibrium seat-vote curve equal to the
30:1099:71270:20:19:95:517:314:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:optimal seat-vote curve, then the social planner can do no better than to choose such a districting.
30:1100:71370:19:19:95:518:295:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:Thefirst analytical achievement of the paper is to show that there exist such districtings if (and
30:1101:71468:19:19:95:517:276:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:only if) the fraction of Independents in the population is not “too large” relative to either the
30:1102:71565:19:19:95:518:257:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:fraction of Democrats or Republicans. These conditions appear permissive and would be satisfied
30:1103:71660:19:19:95:517:238:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:in the vast majority of U.S. States. Moreover, while the analysis does not take into account the
30:1104:71756:19:19:95:518:219:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:geographical constraints faced by officials charged with redistricting in the real world, the optimal
30:1105:71857:19:19:95:517:200:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:seat-vote curve can typically be generated by districtings that look straightforward to achieve.
30:1106:71953:19:20:95:517:181:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:This nurtures the hope that the optimal seat-vote curve may be an attainable benchmark for
30:1107:72043:20:19:95:141:161:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:districters.
30:1108:72055:19:19:110:517:142:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:When the fraction of Independents in the population is large, the optimal seat-vote curve will
30:1109:72149:19:19:95:518:123:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:not be implementable even if the planner has theflexibility in allocating voter types that we have
30:1110:72247:19:19:95:518:104:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:assumed. The second analytical achievement of thepaper is to fully characterize the constrained
30:1111:72342:19:0:95:518:85:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:optimal seat-vote curve. In contrast to the situation when thefirst best is implementable, the
31:1112:72438:0:19:95:518:663:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:constrained optimal seat-vote curve is generated by a unique districting. These optimal districtings
31:1113:72538:19:20:95:518:644:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:involve a complex pattern of voter types, with some districts being all Independent and the
31:1114:72629:20:19:95:491:624:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:remainder containing only Independents andDemocrats or Independents and Republicans.
31:1115:72713:19:19:110:518:605:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:While the shape of the constrained optimal seat-vote curve differs from that of the optimal seat-
31:1116:72810:19:19:95:517:586:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:vote curve, they do share several general features,which can be interpreted as lessons for districting
31:1117:72912:19:19:95:517:567:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:practices. While many commentators consider uncompetitive districts to be undesirable from the
31:1118:73006:19:19:95:517:548:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:perspective of democracy, our welfare economic perspective provides general support for a mix of
31:1119:73102:19:19:95:518:529:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:competitive and safe seats. In addition, the analysis provides support for partisan bias as both the
31:1120:73202:19:19:95:517:510:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:optimal and constrained optimal seat-vote curves are typically biased in favor of the party with
31:1121:73298:19:20:95:517:491:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:the largest voter base. Regarding the districtingsunderlying these seat-vote curves, our analysis
31:1122:73395:20:19:95:518:471:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:provides support for districts that are heterogeneous, rather than identical, in their compositions
31:1123:73494:19:19:95:518:452:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:of voter ideology. While the optimal and constrained optimal systems concur on these issues of the
31:1124:73592:19:19:95:518:433:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:number of safe seats, partisan bias, and cross-district heterogeneity, they differ on the appropriate
31:1125:73693:19:19:95:518:414:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:degree of responsiveness. In particular, while thefirst-best system has a constant responsiveness,
31:1126:73791:19:19:95:513:395:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:the constrained optimal seat-vote curve exhibits responsiveness that varies from zero to infinity.
31:1127:73889:19:19:110:518:376:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:The model and techniques developed in this paper can be used to address other districting
31:1128:73978:19:19:95:518:357:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:questions.  One could study the classic questionof optimal partisan gerrymandering by char-
31:1129:74069:19:20:95:517:338:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:acterizing the implementable seat-vote curve that maximizes the expected utility of (say) the
31:1130:74162:20:19:95:517:318:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:Democrats. This requires solving a problem similar to that studied in Section 7, except the objec-
31:1131:74260:19:19:95:517:299:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:tive function would be the expected welfare of the Democrats rather than the population at large.
31:1132:74357:19:19:95:517:280:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:This exercise might be useful for developing predictions concerning the districtings that a partisan
31:1133:74457:19:19:95:517:261:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:redistricting committee might choose. The model would also facilitate a precise understanding of
31:1134:74553:19:19:95:418:242:100:g_d0_f4:49:g_d0_f7:the determinants of the welfare loss associated with partisan districting.26
31:1135:74629:19:19:110:518:223:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:The model can also be used as a basis to empirically estimate and evaluate seat-vote curves.
31:1136:74721:19:20:95:517:204:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:Coate and Knight (2005) use the model to developan empirical methodology for estimating
31:1137:74808:20:19:95:517:184:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:seat-vote curves for the U.S. States and measuring citizen welfare. This allows the comparison
31:1138:74902:19:19:95:518:165:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:of actual and optimal seat-vote curves and the estimation of the welfare loss associated with
31:1139:74995:19:19:95:518:146:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:observed districtings. Given our argument that it may be reasonably easy to achieve the optimal
31:1140:75090:19:19:95:517:127:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:relationship between seats and votes, we might hope this welfare loss to be small.  Following
31:1141:75183:19:13:103:518:108:36:g_d0_f8:65:g_d0_f9:26It would also be interesting to explore the determinants of the level of partisan bias under the optimal partisan
31:1142:75298:13:0:95:280:95:65:g_d0_f9:65:g_d0_f9:gerrymander as in Gilligan and Matsusaka [1999].
32:1143:75348:0:19:95:517:663:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:King (1989) and Gelman and King (1994), one could also investigate the correlation between
32:1144:75438:19:20:95:275:644:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:redistricting institutions and welfare loss.
32:1145:75482:20:19:110:517:624:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:Finally, it will be clear to the reader that this paper is very much afirst cut at the problem
32:1146:75576:19:19:95:518:605:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:and there are numerous ways the model could usefully be extended. First, it would be interesting
32:1147:75672:19:19:95:517:586:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:to see how strategic voting of the sort discussed in the split-ticket voting literature (Alesina and
32:1148:75772:19:19:95:518:567:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:Rosenthal (1995) and Fiorina (1992)) would impact the analysis.  Second, it would be highly
32:1149:75863:19:19:95:517:548:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:desirable to be able to incorporate geographic constraints in a meaningful way. Perhaps the most
32:1150:75959:19:19:95:517:529:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:fruitful approach would be to devise a way of studying the welfare consequences of local changes
32:1151:76055:19:19:95:517:510:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:in districting. Third, it would be useful to incorporate a governor or president into the model.
32:1152:76151:19:20:95:518:491:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:Fourth, it would be interesting to make the model dynamic and incorporate incumbency.  In
32:1153:76240:20:19:95:518:471:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:reality, incumbents have a significant advantage (perhaps due to greater experience) and, it is
32:1154:76335:19:19:95:517:452:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:often argued that redistricting is done with an eye to preserving the seats of incumbents. Fifth,
32:1155:76432:19:19:95:517:433:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:it would be interesting to give parties a strategic role in terms of candidate selection, perhaps by
32:1156:76532:19:0:95:427:414:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:assuming that they can choose between moderate and extremist candidates.

41:1623:89263:20:19:95:518:410:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:Democrats as possible from the set of districtings that both generate the inverse seat-vote curve
41:1624:89360:19:19:95:518:391:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:and satisfy the constraint that the fraction of Independents used equalsπI. Precisely what that
41:1625:89455:19:19:95:517:372:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:districting looks like will depend upon the actual fraction of Independents available. In case (i)
41:1626:89553:19:19:95:517:353:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:of the Lemma, there are a large fraction of Independents available, and it is optimal to set the
41:1627:89649:19:19:95:521:334:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:fractions of Independents in both the safeDemocrat and competitive districts (πIandπI(i)for
41:1628:89740:19:19:95:518:315:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:alli∈[i,i]) equal to their maximal level, with the remaining Independents allocated to the safe
41:1629:89835:19:19:95:517:296:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:Republican districts. The opposite extreme is case (iv), in which there are only a small fraction
41:1630:89932:19:20:95:518:277:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:of Independents available and it is only in Republican-leaning competitive districts (i∈[i∗∗,i])
41:1631:90028:20:19:95:518:257:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:that the fractions of Independents are set equal totheir maximal level. In all other districts, the
41:1632:90127:19:19:95:517:238:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:fraction of Independents equals its minimal level - which is 0. Cases (ii) and (iii) lie in between
41:1633:90226:19:19:95:162:219:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:these extremes.
41:1634:90241:19:19:110:518:200:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:The nature of the solution to the maximization problem can be deduced from the observation
41:1635:90331:19:19:95:518:181:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:that selecting the districting inG∗(i,i, V∗(·)) that has the maximal fraction of Democrats is
41:1636:90424:19:19:95:517:162:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:equivalent to choosing the districting that has the minimal fraction of Republicans.  One can
41:1637:90517:19:19:95:518:143:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:alternatively define the seat-vote curve as representing the relationship between the fraction of
41:1638:90614:19:20:95:517:124:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f11:seats held by the Republican Party and its share of the aggregate vote. Let such aRepublican
41:1639:90706:20:19:95:518:104:100:g_d0_f11:100:g_d0_f4:seat-vote curvebe denoted bySR(VR), whereSRis the fraction of seats held by Republicans
41:1640:90793:19:0:95:518:85:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:andVRis the fraction of votes they received.  We can analogously defineVRandVRto be
42:1641:90878:0:19:95:518:663:100:g_d0_f4:100:g_d0_f4:the minimal and maximal vote shares received by the Republican Party. Associated with this
